# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Architecture Document: Istio Pilot Discovery Service

**Repository:** istio/istio
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for **Istio Pilot's Discovery Service** subsystem. The document must explain how Pilot serves xDS (Envoy Discovery Service) configuration to proxies, translates Istio's high-level configuration into Envoy-specific resources, integrates with service registries, and supports multi-cluster deployments. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server
The central component implementing Pilot's gRPC interface for Envoy's xDS APIs. Explain:
- How it implements Envoy's xDS v3 protocol (ADS, incremental/state-of-the-world modes)
- The role of `adsClients` in tracking active proxy connections
- How configuration pushes are coordinated: debouncing, rate limiting, concurrent push limits
- Cache management for xDS resources (CDS, LDS, RDS, EDS)
- The lifecycle: initialization, handling new connections, shutdown

### 2. ADS and the Connection Model
The Aggregated Discovery Service stream handler. Explain:
- How `Stream()` establishes a bidirectional gRPC stream with an Envoy proxy
- The `Connection` type: wrapping the stream with proxy metadata and state
- Request processing: how `processRequest()` determines what configuration to send
- Push coordination: how `pushConnection()` transmits updates to a single proxy
- The `StartPush()` broadcast mechanism for fleet-wide updates

### 3. PushContext — Configuration Snapshot and Translation
The immutable configuration snapshot used during a push. Explain:
- What `PushContext` holds: services, destination rules, virtual services, sidecars, gateways
- How `InitContext()` rebuilds the push context when Istio config changes (CRD watches)
- Config translation: how Pilot converts Istio's `VirtualService` and `DestinationRule` into Envoy's `RouteConfiguration` and `Cluster` resources
- The relationship between push triggers (config changes, service registry updates) and push context regeneration
- Metrics and error tracking during push generation

### 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support
The service discovery layer feeding the DiscoveryServer. Explain:
- How `ServiceRegistry` (Kubernetes controller) watches K8s Services, Endpoints, and Pods
- The aggregate controller pattern for multi-registry support (K8s services + `ServiceEntry` resources)
- Multi-cluster support: how Pilot aggregates services from multiple clusters
- How endpoint updates (pod scale-up, health changes) trigger EDS pushes
- The relationship between the service registry and xDS: when does a service change trigger CDS vs. EDS?

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path from Istio config change → DiscoveryServer → xDS push to Envoy proxies
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Istio (custom config translation, external service registries, telemetry plugins)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (config validation, push failures, proxy disconnects) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the istio/istio repository (e.g., `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`, `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`)

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or struct dump
- Do NOT fabricate type names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Istio components outside the Pilot discovery path (e.g., Citadel, Galley, sidecar injection)

59-assistanttext-
The architecture document has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here's a summary of what it covers:

---

## Document Summary

The document explains four interlocking components and how they work together:

### 1. DiscoveryServer (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`)
The singleton gRPC server and orchestrator. It owns the live `adsClients` map, the two-stage pipeline (debounce `pushChannel` → ordered `pushQueue`), the concurrent push semaphore, and the typed LRU `Cache`. The debounce loop merges rapid config changes into single push context rebuilds; the `sendPushes` loop dispatches work to individual proxy goroutines.

### 2. ADS / Connection (`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`, `delta.go`)
Each connected Envoy proxy gets a `Connection` wrapping the gRPC stream with its `proxy` metadata and per-type watched resource state. The document explains the initialization race-condition safety (`addCon` before `MarkInitialized`), how `processRequest` handles ACK/NACK nonces, and why resources are pushed in the strict `CDS → EDS → LDS → RDS → SDS` order.

### 3. PushContext (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`)
The immutable per-push snapshot. `InitContext` does a full rebuild or an incremental update (only re-indexing the sub-structures whose config kinds appear in `ConfigsUpdated`). The document traces how VirtualService and DestinationRule are indexed, how SidecarScope scopes service visibility, and how generator code in `pilot/pkg/networking/core/` reads these indexes to produce Envoy `Cluster`, `RouteConfiguration`, and `Listener` protos.

### 4. Service Registry (`kube/controller/`, `aggregate/`)
The Kubernetes `Controller` watches Services, EndpointSlices, and Pods. Endpoint changes call `EDSUpdate` (incremental push, no push context rebuild) while service deletions/additions cal
... (truncated)

Original code avoided the mutexes by doing both 'push' and 'process requests' in same thread.\\n138: func (s *DiscoveryServer) processRequest(req *discovery.DiscoveryRequest, con *Connection) error {\\n139: \\tstype := v3.GetShortType(req.TypeUrl)\\n140: \\tlog.Debugf(\\\"ADS:%s: REQ %s resources:%d nonce:%s version:%s \\\", stype,\\n141: \\t\\tcon.ID(), len(req.ResourceNames), req.ResponseNonce, req.VersionInfo)\\n142: \\tif req.TypeUrl == v3.HealthInfoType {\\n143: \\t\\ts.handleWorkloadHealthcheck(con.proxy, req)\\n144: \\t\\treturn nil\\n145: \\t}\\n146: \\n147: \\t// For now, don't let xDS piggyback debug requests start watchers.\\n148: \\tif strings.HasPrefix(req.TypeUrl, v3.DebugType) {\\n149: \\t\\treturn s.pushXds(con,\\n150: \\t\\t\\t&model.WatchedResource{TypeUrl: req.TypeUrl, ResourceNames: sets.New(req.ResourceNames...)},\\n151: \\t\\t\\t&model.PushRequest{Full: true, Push: con.proxy.LastPushContext, Forced: true})\\n152: \\t}\\n153: \\n154: \\tshouldRespond, delta := xds.ShouldRespond(con.proxy, con.ID(), req)\\n155: \\tif !shouldRespond {\\n156: \\t\\treturn nil\\n157: \\t}\\n158: \\n159: \\trequest := &model.PushRequest{\\n160: \\t\\tFull:   true,\\n161: \\t\\tPush:   con.proxy.LastPushContext,\\n162: \\t\\tReason: model.NewReasonStats(model.ProxyRequest),\\n163: \\n164: \\t\\t// The usage of LastPushTime (rather than time.Now()), is critical here for correctness; This time\\n165: \\t\\t// is used by the XDS cache to determine if a entry is stale. During\\n190: \\t\\t// loading request, concurrency=1. Once that request is done, concurrency is enabled.\\n191: \\t\\t// However, the XDS stream is long lived, so the first request would block all others. As a\\n192: \\t\\t// result, we should exit the first request immediately; clients will retry.\\n193: \\t\\tfirstRequest.Store(false)\\n194: \\t\\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \\\"server warmup not complete; try again\\\")\\n195: \\t}\\n196: \\t// Check if server is ready to accept clients and process new requests.\\n197: \\t// Currently ready means caches have been synced and hence can build\\n198: \\t// clusters correctly. Without this check, InitContext() call below would\\n199: \\t// initialize with empty config, leading to reconnected Envoys losing\\n200: \\t// configuration. This is an additional safety check inaddition to adding\\n201: \\t// cachesSynced logic to readiness probe to handle cases where kube-proxy\\n202: \\t// ip tables update latencies.\\n203: \\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/25495.\\n204: \\tif !s.IsServerReady() {\\n205: \\t\\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \\\"server is not ready to serve discovery information\\\")\\n206: \\t}\\n207: \\n208: \\tctx := stream.Context()\\n209: \\tpeerAddr := \\\"0.0.0.0\\\"\\n210: \\tif peerInfo, ok := peer.FromContext(ctx); During\n190: \t\t// loading request, concurrency=1. Once that request is done, concurrency is enabled.\n191: \t\t// However, the XDS stream is long lived, so the first request would block all others. As a\n192: \t\t// result, we should exit the first request immediately; clients will retry.\n193: \t\tfirstRequest.Store(false)\n194: \t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \"server warmup not complete; try again\")\n195: \t}\n196: \t// Check if server is ready to accept clients and process new requests.\n197: \t// Currently ready means caches have been synced and hence can build\n198: \t// clusters correctly. Without this check, InitContext() call below would\n199: \t// initialize with empty config, leading to reconnected Envoys losing\n200: \t// configuration. This is an additional safety check inaddition to adding\n201: \t// cachesSynced logic to readiness probe to handle cases where kube-proxy\n202: \t// ip tables update latencies.\n203: \t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/25495.\n204: \tif !s.IsServerReady() {\n205: \t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \"server is not ready to serve discovery information\")\n206: \t}\n207: \n208: \tctx := stream.Context()\n209: \tpeerAddr := \"0.0.0.0\"\n210: \tif peerInfo, ok := peer.FromContext(ctx); namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\n312: \n313: // XDSUpdater is used for direct updates of the xDS model and incremental push.\n314: // Pilot uses multiple registries - for example each K8S cluster is a registry\n315: // instance. Each registry is responsible for tracking a set\n316: // of endpoints associated with mesh services, and calling the EDSUpdate on changes.\n317: // A registry may group endpoints for a service in smaller subsets - for example by\n318: // deployment, or to deal with very large number of endpoints for a service. We want\n319: // to avoid passing around large objects - like full list of endpoints for a registry,\n320: // or the full list of endpoints for a service across registries, since it limits\n321: // scalability.\n322: //\n323: // Future optimizations will include grouping the endpoints by labels, gateway or region to\n324: // reduce the time when subsetting or split-horizon is used. {
  "content": "# Istio Pilot Discovery Service: Architecture Document\n\n## Overview\n\nPilot's discovery subsystem is the core of Istio's control plane. It translates high-level mesh configuration (VirtualService, DestinationRule, ServiceEntry, etc.) into Envoy's native xDS resources (CDS, LDS, RDS, EDS) and streams them to every proxy in the mesh over long-lived gRPC connections. Four interlocking components make this work:\n\n1. **DiscoveryServer** \u2014 the gRPC server and orchestrator\n2. **ADS/Connection** \u2014 the per-proxy stream handler\n3. **PushContext** \u2014 an immutable configuration snapshot built once per change event\n4. **Service Registry** \u2014 the Kubernetes and ServiceEntry watchers that feed discovery data\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer \u2014 The xDS gRPC Server\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\n### What it owns\n\n`DiscoveryServer` is the singleton struct that implements Envoy's `AggregatedDiscoveryService` gRPC interface. It is the authoritative owner of:\n\n- `adsClients map[string]*Connection` \u2014 the live set of connected Envoy proxies, keyed by connection ID\n- `pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest` \u2014 raw incoming change notifications (from config watches, service registry, JWT resolver, etc.)\n- `pushQueue *PushQueue` \u2014 ordered work queue for per-proxy push dispatch after debouncing\n- `Cache model.XdsCache` \u2014 typed LRU cache for already-generated xDS resources\n- `concurrentPushLimit chan struct{}` \u2014 semaphore that caps parallel in-flight pushes (controlled by `PILOT_PUSH_THROTTLE`)\n- `RequestRateLimit *rate.Limiter` \u2014 token bucket that throttles new gRPC connection acceptance\n\n### Initialization and startup\n\n`NewDiscoveryServer` creates the struct and wires its fields. No resources are served until `CachesSynced()` is called, which sets `serverReady = true`. Until that point, every incoming connection receives `codes.Unavailable`. The `Start()` method launches four background goroutines:\n\n```\nStart()\n  \u251c\u2500 WorkloadEntryController.Run(stopCh)    // auto-registration of VMs\n  \u251c\u2500 handleUpdates(stopCh)                  // debounce loop\n  \u251c\u2500 periodicRefreshMetrics(stopCh)         // prometheus push-status gauge\n  \u2514\u2500 sendPushes(stopCh)                     // dispatch loop\n```\n\n### Debounce loop\n\nAll change events arrive via `ConfigUpdate(req *model.PushRequest)`, which writes to `pushChannel`. The `handleUpdates` goroutine runs `debounce()` over that channel:\n\n- If `DebounceAfter` (default 100ms) passes without a new event, the accumulated `PushRequest` (merged from all arrivals) is forwarded to `Push()`.\n- If `debounceMax` (default 10s) elapses with a constant event stream, the push is forced regardless.\n- EDS-only pushes (non-full) bypass debouncing and are forwarded immediately unless `PILOT_ENABLE_EDS_DEBOUNCE=true`.\n\nMultiple `PushRequest` values that arrive during the quiet window are merged via `PushRequest.Merge()`, which unions `ConfigsUpdated` sets and ORs the `Full` flag. This ensures that even if ten resources changed, only one push context rebuild happens.\n\n### Concurrent push dispatch\n\n`sendPushes()` \u2192 `doSendPushes()` reads from `pushQueue` and runs pushes concurrently, gated by `concurrentPushLimit`. Each dequeued push is sent as an `Event` to the target connection's `PushCh()` channel. If the gRPC stream has already closed, the event is dropped and `doneFunc()` releases the semaphore slot.\n\n### XDS resource cache\n\n`Cache` (type `model.XdsCache`, implemented in `pilot/pkg/model/typed_xds_cache.go`) is a typed LRU keyed by a hash of the proxy identity and resource type. Each entry records its _dependent configs_ \u2014 the set of Istio resource hashes that were consulted during generation. When `dropCacheForRequest()` is called:\n\n- **Full push with `Forced=true`** \u2192 `Cache.ClearAll()` evicts everything.\n- **Scoped full push** \u2192 `Cache.Clear(req.ConfigsUpdated)` walks the config index and evicts only entries whose dependent configs overlap with the changed set.\n\nConcurrent writers may both get a cache miss and generate identical configuration; `assertUnchanged` (active when `PILOT_ENABLE_UNSAFE_ASSERTIONS=true`) detects non-deterministic generation.\n\n### Generator registry\n\n`DiscoveryServer.Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator` maps type URLs (and optionally proxy-type/type-URL compound keys) to generators. At startup, Istiod registers:\n\n| Key | Generator |\n|---|---|\n| `cluster.loadassignment.v3.ClusterLoadAssignment` (EDS) | `EdsGenerator` |\n| `listener.v3.Listener` (LDS) | `ListenerGenerator` |\n| `route.v3.RouteConfiguration` (RDS) | `RouteConfigGenerator` |\n| `cluster.v3.Cluster` (CDS) | `ClusterGenerator` |\n| `secret.v3.Secret` (SDS) | `SecretGenerator` |\n| Custom proxy generators (Ztunnel, ambient) | registered on first use |\n\nThe `findGenerator()` function in `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go` resolves the most-specific generator: `metadata.Generator/typeURL` \u2192 `proxy.Type/typeURL` \u2192 `typeURL` \u2192 proxy-default.\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n**Sources:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`\n\n### Stream establishment\n\n`StreamAggregatedResources(stream)` (state-of-the-world ADS) and `DeltaAggregatedResources(stream)` (incremental xDS) are the two gRPC entry points. Both share the same lifecycle:\n\n1. **Rate-limit check** \u2014 `WaitForRequestLimit` blocks if the token bucket is exhausted (returning `codes.ResourceExhausted`).\n2. **mTLS authentication** \u2014 `s.authenticate(ctx)` extracts peer certificate SANs from gRPC metadata. Failure returns `codes.Unauthenticated`.\n3. **Connection creation** \u2014 a `Connection` struct wraps the raw gRPC stream. The connection is anonymous until the first `DiscoveryRequest` arrives with a `node` field.\n4. **Readiness guard** \u2014 if `serverReady` is false, the connection is rejected.\n\n### The `Connection` type\n\n```go\ntype Connection struct {\n    xds.Connection                // stream wrapper, push channel, watched resource state\n    node        *core.Node        // raw envoy node metadata (preserved to avoid re-marshal)\n    proxy       *model.Proxy      // fully parsed, enriched proxy object\n    deltaStream DeltaDiscoveryStream\n    deltaReqChan chan *discovery.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\n    s           *DiscoveryServer\n}\n```\n\n`xds.Connection` (in `pkg/xds`) holds:\n- The gRPC stream\n- `WatchedResources map[string]*model.WatchedResource` \u2014 per-type subscription state\n- `PushCh() chan any` \u2014 the channel through which push events are delivered to this connection's goroutine\n\n### Proxy initialization\n\n`initConnection(node, con, identities)` performs the full lifecycle in order:\n\n1. `initProxyMetadata` \u2014 parses `node.Metadata` and `node.Id` into a `model.Proxy`. Fails fast with `codes.InvalidArgument` on bad format.\n2. Cluster alias resolution \u2014 remaps the proxy's cluster ID if configured.\n3. `addCon(con.ID(), con)` \u2014 registers the connection in `adsClients` **before** completing initialization, to avoid a race with new push contexts arriving between registration and initialization.\n4. `authorize(con, identities)` \u2014 enforces RBAC rules on the peer identities.\n5. `initializeProxy(con)` \u2014 calls `computeProxyState`, discovers IP mode, assigns the default generator.\n6. `con.MarkInitialized()` \u2014 signals that the proxy is safe to push to.\n\n### Request processing\n\nEvery inbound `DiscoveryRequest` flows through `processRequest(req, con)`:\n\n- **HealthInfo requests** \u2014 dispatched to `WorkloadEntryController` for VM health-check recording; no xDS response.\n- **Debug type URLs** \u2014 answered immediately with a forced full push of the requested debug resource.\n- **Normal type URLs** \u2014 `ShouldRespond()` checks the ACK/NACK nonce logic to decide if a response is warranted. If yes, a `PushRequest{Full: true, Reason: ProxyRequest}` is built and `pushXds` is called.\n\n### Push ordering\n\n`pushConnection()` iterates over `watchedResourcesByOrder()`, which returns watched resources sorted by `PushOrder`:\n\n```go\nvar PushOrder = []string{\n    v3.ClusterType,    // CDS first \u2014 clusters must exist before listeners reference them\n    v3.EndpointType,   // EDS\n    v3.ListenerType,   // LDS\n    v3.RouteType,      // RDS\n    v3.SecretType,     // SDS\n    v3.AddressType,    // ambient workload addresses\n    v3.WorkloadType,\n    v3.WorkloadAuthorizationType,\n}\n```\n\nThis ordering is critical: an Envoy proxy will reject a listener that references a cluster it has not yet received.\n\n### `StartPush` \u2014 fleet-wide broadcast\n\n`AdsPushAll(req)` \u2192 `StartPush(req)` iterates over `AllClients()` and calls `pushQueue.Enqueue(con, req)` for every connection. `PushQueue` is a FIFO work queue with merge semantics: if a connection is already pending or in-flight, the new request is merged rather than enqueued twice. This prevents a wave of endpoint changes from generating N independent pushes per proxy.\n\n### Incremental (Delta) xDS\n\n`delta.go` implements `StreamDeltas` using `DeltaDiscoveryRequest`/`DeltaDiscoveryResponse`. In delta mode, the client sends explicit subscribe/unsubscribe resource names. `EdsGenerator.GenerateDeltas` can take advantage of this to compute only added/removed endpoints (`buildDeltaEndpoints`), reducing response payload size. For most resource types, delta falls back to state-of-the-world generation with the delta information used only to filter which resources to include.\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext \u2014 Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`\n\n### What PushContext holds\n\n`PushContext` is the immutable global snapshot of all mesh configuration, rebuilt on every full push. It is the single source of truth used during xDS generation:\n\n| Field | Content |\n|---|---|\n| `ServiceIndex` | All services, indexed by hostname, namespace, and exportTo visibility |\n| `virtualServiceIndex` | VirtualServices indexed by gateway and namespace for fast lookup |\n| `destinationRuleIndex` | DestinationRules indexed by hostname and namespace, with wildcard support |\n| `sidecarIndex` | SidecarScope objects pre-computed per namespace |\n| `gatewayIndex` | Gateways indexed by namespace |\n| `envoyFiltersByNamespace` | EnvoyFilter patches grouped by namespace |\n| `wasmPluginsByNamespace` | WasmPlugin extensions grouped by namespace |\n| `AuthnPolicies` | PeerAuthentication and RequestAuthentication |\n| `AuthzPolicies` | AuthorizationPolicy |\n| `Telemetry` | Telemetry resources |\n| `Mesh` | The global `MeshConfig` |\n| `networkMgr` | Cross-network gateway addresses |\n\n### `InitContext` and incremental rebuild\n\n`InitContext(env, oldPushContext, pushReq)` is the entry point. It is idempotent (`InitDone` atomic flag) and mutex-protected.\n\n- **Full rebuild** (`pushReq == nil` or `Forced=true`): calls `createNewContext`, which initializes every index from scratch: services \u2192 Kubernetes gateways \u2192 VirtualServices \u2192 DestinationRules \u2192 AuthN \u2192 AuthZ \u2192 Telemetry \u2192 WasmPlugins \u2192 EnvoyFilters \u2192 Gateways \u2192 SidecarScopes (last, because they depend on services and VSes).\n- **Incremental rebuild** (`updateContext`): inspects `pushReq.ConfigsUpdated` and only re-initializes the index whose config kind changed. If only `DestinationRule` changed, `initDestinationRules` runs, but `initVirtualServices` is skipped and the old index is shallow-copied. This avoids full re-index for unrelated changes.\n\nThe incremental update logic maps config kinds to dirty flags:\n\n```\nServiceEntry / DNSName       \u2192 servicesChanged\nDestinationRule              \u2192 destinationRulesChanged\nVirtualService               \u2192 virtualServicesChanged\nGateway                      \u2192 gatewayChanged\nSidecar                      \u2192 sidecarsChanged\nEnvoyFilter                  \u2192 envoyFiltersChanged\nAuthorizationPolicy          \u2192 authzChanged\nRequestAuthentication /\n  PeerAuthentication         \u2192 authnChanged\n```\n\nSidecarScope is recomputed whenever services, virtual services, destination rules, or sidecars change, because all four affect egress listener reachability.\n\n### SidecarScope and service visibility\n\n`getSidecarScope(proxy, workloadLabels)` selects or lazily computes a `SidecarScope` for the proxy's namespace. It controls which services are visible in that proxy's egress listeners. The three cases:\n\n1. **User-defined Sidecar in proxy namespace** \u2014 matched by workload selector labels. First exact match wins.\n2. **Root-namespace Sidecar** (`istio-system`) \u2014 converted to per-namespace scopes on demand, cached in `meshRootSidecarsByNamespace`.\n3. **Default scope** \u2014 `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace`, which grants access to all mesh services. Cached in `defaultSidecarsByNamespace`. Gateways use `DefaultSidecarScopeForGateway`.\n\nThe lazy caching pattern means that namespace-scoped defaults are only allocated for namespaces that actually have connected proxies.\n\n### DestinationRule resolution\n\n`destinationRule(proxyNamespace, service)` implements a four-step precedence lookup:\n\n1. Proxy's own namespace (most specific override)\n2. Service's namespace (producer policy)\n3. Root namespace (global default)\n\n`MostSpecificHostMatch` distinguishes between exact and wildcard host patterns, preferring exact matches.\n\n### Config translation: VirtualService \u2192 Envoy RouteConfiguration\n\nConfig translation is performed by generators in `pilot/pkg/networking/core/`:\n\n- **CDS** (`cds.go`): for each service visible to a proxy, `buildOutboundCluster` reads the matching `DestinationRule` from the push context to configure TLS settings, load balancing policy, connection pool, and subset-level clusters. The result is an Envoy `Cluster` proto.\n- **RDS** (`route/route.go`): `buildSidecarOutboundRouteConfig` reads `VirtualService`s from the push context via `SidecarScope.services` and `VirtualServicesForGateway`, then translates HTTP match conditions, retries, timeouts, fault injection, and mirror rules into Envoy `RouteConfiguration` protos.\n- **LDS** (`listener_builder.go`): creates virtual outbound listener per port based on the sidecar scope, selecting HTTP vs. TCP filter chains from service protocol.\n- **EDS** (`pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`): reads live endpoint shards directly from `model.EndpointIndex` (not the push context), enabling EDS to be incremental without a full push context rebuild.\n\n### Metrics and error tracking\n\n`PushContext.ProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus` accumulates per-proxy anomalies during generation (e.g., `EndpointNoPod`, `ProxyStatusClusterNoInstances`, `DuplicatedClusters`). These are written via `AddMetric(metric, key, proxyID, msg)` from inside generators. `OnConfigChange()` and `UpdateMetrics()` publish these to Prometheus gauges (e.g., `pilot_no_ip`, `pilot_duplicate_envoy_clusters`). The periodic goroutine in `DiscoveryServer` logs the `StatusJSON()` payload every 10 seconds if it changed.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n**Sources:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go`, `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\n### Kubernetes controller\n\n`Controller` (in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/`) is the Kubernetes service registry. For each cluster, one `Controller` instance is created. It watches:\n\n- `v1.Service` \u2192 `onServiceEvent` \u2192 `SvcUpdate` (tells xDS that cluster/EDS membership may change)\n- `EndpointSlice` \u2192 `endpointSliceController` \u2192 `EDSUpdate` / `EDSCacheUpdate`\n- `v1.Pod` \u2192 `PodCache` \u2192 feeds endpoint builder with pod labels and node locality\n- `v1.Node` \u2192 `onNodeEvent` \u2192 updates `nodeInfoMap` for gateway address resolution\n\nEach watcher registers handlers via `registerHandlers`, which push work items onto a rate-limited `queue.Instance`. The queue serializes changes within a cluster, preventing concurrent mutations to `servicesMap`.\n\nWhen an `EndpointSlice` event fires, `buildIstioEndpoints` constructs `model.IstioEndpoint` objects enriched with pod labels, network, locality, and service account. These are then passed to `EDSUpdate` or `EDSCacheUpdate` on the `XDSUpdater` interface (which `DiscoveryServer` satisfies).\n\n### XDSUpdater interface \u2014 the boundary between registry and xDS\n\n```go\ntype XDSUpdater interface {\n    EDSUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\n    EDSCacheUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\n    SvcUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, event Event)\n    ConfigUpdate(req *PushRequest)\n    ProxyUpdate(clusterID cluster.ID, ip string)\n    RemoveShard(shardKey ShardKey)\n}\n```\n\n`EDSUpdate` updates the `EndpointIndex` and triggers an **incremental push** (non-full `PushRequest`). Incremental pushes skip push context rebuild, update only EDS resources, and flow through the debouncer only if EDS debounce is enabled. This is how pod scale-up events propagate to envoys within milliseconds without rebuilding the entire config graph.\n\n`EDSCacheUpdate` updates `EndpointIndex` without triggering a push \u2014 used when many endpoints are changing atomically (e.g., during initial cache sync) to batch updates into a single eventual `EDSUpdate`.\n\n`SvcUpdate` is called when a Kubernetes `Service` is added/deleted. A service deletion calls `EndpointIndex.DeleteServiceShard`, and the service change triggers a **full push** (which rebuilds push context, regenerates CDS, LDS, RDS).\n\n### When service changes trigger CDS vs. EDS\n\n| Change | Push Type | Explanation |\n|---|---|---|\n| Pod added/removed (EndpointSlice update) | Incremental (EDS only) | Only load assignment changes; clusters/listeners unchanged |\n| Service added/deleted | Full push | CDS clusters must be created or removed; LDS may need new listener ports |\n| DestinationRule change | Full push | Cluster TLS/LB configuration changes; CDS must regenerate |\n| VirtualService change | Full push | Route configurations change; RDS must regenerate |\n| ServiceEntry added | Full push | New synthetic service \u2192 new clusters and routes |\n\nThe `edsNeedsPush` function in `eds.go` enforces this: it skips EDS generation for config kinds listed in `skippedEdsConfigs` (Gateway, VirtualService, AuthorizationPolicy, etc.), ensuring EDS only fires for changes that actually affect endpoint membership.\n\n### Aggregate controller\n\n`aggregate.Controller` (in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`) implements `model.ServiceDiscovery` by delegating to a slice of `registryEntry` objects. Each registry entry corresponds to one cluster (Kubernetes) or the ServiceEntry registry. Methods like `Services()`, `InstancesByPort()`, and `GetProxyServiceTargets()` iterate over all registries and merge results.\n\nFor multi-cluster scenarios, when `AddRegistry` is called for a remote cluster's Kubernetes controller, that cluster's services and endpoints become visible to the aggregate. Each `Controller` shard tags its endpoints with `ShardKey{Cluster: clusterID, Provider: Kubernetes}`, allowing `EndpointIndex` to track which shard owns which endpoints.\n\n### Multi-cluster support\n\n`Multicluster` (in `multicluster.go`) manages the lifecycle of per-cluster `kubeController` instances. It uses `multicluster.Component` to watch remote cluster Secrets (which contain kubeconfig files) and create or destroy `Controller` instances accordingly. When a cluster is removed, `kubeController.Close()`:\n\n1. Unregisters the cluster's event handlers from the aggregate controller\n2. Deletes its registry from the aggregate\n3. Triggers a full push (`ClusterUpdate` reason) so all proxies see the cluster removed\n\nThis allows Istiod to react to cluster membership changes without restarting. The `ClusterAliases` map (on `DiscoveryServer`) handles cases where a proxy connects with a cluster ID that is known under a different alias.\n\n### ServiceEntry controller\n\n`serviceentry.Controller` (in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/`) registers itself as a config store watcher and translates `ServiceEntry` CRDs into `model.Service` + `model.IstioEndpoint` objects, then calls `EDSUpdate`/`SvcUpdate` on the `XDSUpdater`. This is how external services (databases, external APIs) and VM workloads appear in the mesh alongside Kubernetes services.\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Config Change \u2192 xDS Push\n\n```\n[K8s/CRD watch]         [Service registry event]\n       \u2502                         \u2502\nConfigUpdate(Full)        EDSUpdate / SvcUpdate\n       \u2502                         \u2502\n       \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                  \u25bc\n          pushChannel (buffered, 10)\n                  \u2502\n          debounce() goroutine\n          (merges concurrent requests, waits DebounceAfter)\n                  \u2502\n          Push(mergedPushRequest)\n                  \u2502\n          \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n          \u2502 Full push?       \u2502 Incremental (EDS)?\n          \u2502                  \u2502\n    initPushContext()    use existing PushContext\n    (rebuilds indexes    dropCacheForRequest()\n     selectively)        AdsPushAll()\n          \u2502                  \u2502\n          \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                 \u25bc\n          StartPush(req)\n          (enqueues req for every connected proxy)\n                 \u2502\n          sendPushes() / doSendPushes()\n          (concurrentPushLimit semaphore)\n                 \u2502\n          client.PushCh() <- &Event{pushRequest}\n                 \u2502\n          pushConnection(con, ev)\n          \u251c\u2500 computeProxyState(proxy, req)   [if Full]\n          \u251c\u2500 ProxyNeedsPush(proxy, req)      [skip if irrelevant]\n          \u2514\u2500 for each watched resource (ordered CDS\u2192EDS\u2192LDS\u2192RDS):\n               pushXds(con, watchedResource, req)\n               \u251c\u2500 findGenerator(typeURL)\n               \u251c\u2500 gen.Generate(proxy, w, req)  [may cache hit or miss]\n               \u2514\u2500 xds.Send(con, DiscoveryResponse)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\n### 1. Custom resource generators\n\nRegister a `model.XdsResourceGenerator` (or `XdsDeltaResourceGenerator`) in `DiscoveryServer.Generators`. The key format `\"<proxyType>/<typeURL>\"` allows per-proxy-type overrides. This is how Ztunnel (`Ztunnel` proxy type) gets completely different configuration from sidecar proxies for the same type URLs.\n\n### 2. EnvoyFilter patching\n\nAfter generation, each generator applies `MergedEnvoyFilterWrapper` patches from the push context. Patches can add, merge, or remove fields at specific listener/cluster/route filter chain points. This is the primary mechanism for customizing generated Envoy config without modifying Pilot source code.\n\n### 3. WasmPlugin extensions\n\n`WasmPlugin` resources are loaded into the push context and applied by the networking layer as `wasm` HTTP filters. Each plugin specifies a selector, phase, and priority, so multiple plugins compose predictably.\n\n### 4. External service registries\n\nAny component that implements `model.ServiceDiscovery` can be registered with the aggregate controller via `AddRegistry`. MCP (Mesh Configuration Protocol) sources, for example, can inject synthetic services this way.\n\n### 5. `ProxyNeedsPush` hook\n\n`DiscoveryServer.ProxyNeedsPush func(proxy *model.Proxy, req *model.PushRequest) (*model.PushRequest, bool)` is called for every proxy before any generation work. It can completely skip a push (`bool=false`) or narrow the `ConfigsUpdated` set. The default `DefaultProxyNeedsPush` implements the sidecar scope optimization: if none of the changed configs are reachable from the proxy's sidecar scope, the push is skipped.\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Config validation errors\nIstio CRDs are validated by the admission webhook before reaching the config store. If invalid configuration reaches Pilot anyway (e.g., from a file source), `initVirtualServices` / `initDestinationRules` may log warnings and skip the offending resource. The proxy status metric `DuplicatedDomains` captures rejected VirtualServices.\n\n### Push context rebuild failures\n`createNewContext` and `updateContext` do not return errors; individual sub-initializers log errors and best-effort continue. A malformed DestinationRule will be logged and skipped, leaving the previous rule in effect.\n\n### Push generation errors\nIf `gen.Generate()` returns an error, `pushXds` logs it and returns the error to `pushConnection`, which returns the error to the connection's stream goroutine, closing the stream. The proxy will reconnect and re-subscribe.\n\n### Send failures\n`xds.Send(con, resp)` errors are classified by `recordSendError`: gRPC `codes.Canceled` and `codes.Unavailable` (normal stream close) are silently dropped; other errors are warned. Any error closes the push cycle for that resource on that connection.\n\n### Proxy disconnects\n`closeConnection(con)` removes the connection from `adsClients` and calls `WorkloadEntryController.OnDisconnect`, which may delete the proxy's `WorkloadEntry` if it was auto-registered.\n\n### Cache token staleness\nThe `lruCache.token` field is incremented on `Clear`/`ClearAll`. Each cached entry records the token at write time. On `Add`, if the current token is greater than the entry's token, the write is silently dropped, preventing stale results from a slow goroutine overwriting fresh results from a faster concurrent push.\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files Reference\n\n| File | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go` | `DiscoveryServer` struct, debounce loop, push orchestration, cache management |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` | `Connection` type, `Stream()`, `processRequest()`, `pushConnection()`, `StartPush()`, `AdsPushAll()` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go` | Delta (incremental) xDS stream handler |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go` | Generator lookup (`findGenerator`), `pushXds`, `xdsNeedsPush` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/pushqueue.go` | `PushQueue` \u2014 merge-on-enqueue work queue |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go` | `EdsGenerator`, `EDSUpdate`, `EDSCacheUpdate`, `SvcUpdate` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go` | `ClusterGenerator` entry point |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go` | `ListenerGenerator` entry point |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go` | `RouteGenerator` entry point |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` | `PushContext`, `InitContext`, `updateContext`, `XDSUpdater` interface, `PushRequest`, `TriggerReason` |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/typed_xds_cache.go` | `typedXdsCache`, `lruCache`, config-indexed eviction |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go` | `EndpointIndex`, shard management |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` | `SidecarScope`, `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace` |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go` | Kubernetes `Controller`, service/endpoint/pod watchers |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/multicluster.go` | `Multicluster`, per-cluster controller lifecycle |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go` | Aggregate `Controller`, multi-registry fan-out |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/` | ServiceEntry \u2192 `model.Service` translation |\n| `pilot/pkg/networking/core/` | CDS/LDS/RDS config translation from push context to Envoy protos |\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"

{
  "content": "# Istio Pilot Discovery Service: Architecture Document\n\n## Overview\n\nPilot's discovery subsystem is the core of Istio's control plane. It translates high-level mesh configuration (VirtualService, DestinationRule, ServiceEntry, etc.) into Envoy's native xDS resources (CDS, LDS, RDS, EDS) and streams them to every proxy in the mesh over long-lived gRPC connections. Four interlocking components make this work:\n\n1. **DiscoveryServer** \u2014 the gRPC server and orchestrator\n2. **ADS/Connection** \u2014 the per-proxy stream handler\n3. **PushContext** \u2014 an immutable configuration snapshot built once per change event\n4. **Service Registry** \u2014 the Kubernetes and ServiceEntry watchers that feed discovery data\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer \u2014 The xDS gRPC Server\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\n### What it owns\n\n`DiscoveryServer` is the singleton struct that implements Envoy's `AggregatedDiscoveryService` gRPC interface. It is the authoritative owner of:\n\n- `adsClients map[string]*Connection` \u2014 the live set of connected Envoy proxies, keyed by connection ID\n- `pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest` \u2014 raw incoming change notifications (from config watches, service registry, JWT resolver, etc.)\n- `pushQueue *PushQueue` \u2014 ordered work queue for per-proxy push dispatch after debouncing\n- `Cache model.XdsCache` \u2014 typed LRU cache for already-generated xDS resources\n- `concurrentPushLimit chan struct{}` \u2014 semaphore that caps parallel in-flight pushes (controlled by `PILOT_PUSH_THROTTLE`)\n- `RequestRateLimit *rate.Limiter` \u2014 token bucket that throttles new gRPC connection acceptance\n\n### Initialization and startup\n\n`NewDiscoveryServer` creates the struct and wires its fields. No resources are served until `CachesSynced()` is called, which sets `serverReady = true`. Until that point, every incoming connection receives `codes.Unavailable`. The `Start()` method launches four background goroutines:\n\n```\nStart()\n  \u251c\u2500 WorkloadEntryController.Run(stopCh)    // auto-registration of VMs\n  \u251c\u2500 handleUpdates(stopCh)                  // debounce loop\n  \u251c\u2500 periodicRefreshMetrics(stopCh)         // prometheus push-status gauge\n  \u2514\u2500 sendPushes(stopCh)                     // dispatch loop\n```\n\n### Debounce loop\n\nAll change events arrive via `ConfigUpdate(req *model.PushRequest)`, which writes to `pushChannel`. The `handleUpdates` goroutine runs `debounce()` over that channel:\n\n- If `DebounceAfter` (default 100ms) passes without a new event, the accumulated `PushRequest` (merged from all arrivals) is forwarded to `Push()`.\n- If `debounceMax` (default 10s) elapses with a constant event stream, the push is forced regardless.\n- EDS-only pushes (non-full) bypass debouncing and are forwarded immediately unless `PILOT_ENABLE_EDS_DEBOUNCE=true`.\n\nMultiple `PushRequest` values that arrive during the quiet window are merged via `PushRequest.Merge()`, which unions `ConfigsUpdated` sets and ORs the `Full` flag. This ensures that even if ten resources changed, only one push context rebuild happens.\n\n### Concurrent push dispatch\n\n`sendPushes()` \u2192 `doSendPushes()` reads from `pushQueue` and runs pushes concurrently, gated by `concurrentPushLimit`. Each dequeued push is sent as an `Event` to the target connection's `PushCh()` channel. If the gRPC stream has already closed, the event is dropped and `doneFunc()` releases the semaphore slot.\n\n### XDS resource cache\n\n`Cache` (type `model.XdsCache`, implemented in `pilot/pkg/model/typed_xds_cache.go`) is a typed LRU keyed by a hash of the proxy identity and resource type. Each entry records its _dependent configs_ \u2014 the set of Istio resource hashes that were consulted during generation. When `dropCacheForRequest()` is called:\n\n- **Full push with `Forced=true`** \u2192 `Cache.ClearAll()` evicts everything.\n- **Scoped full push** \u2192 `Cache.Clear(req.ConfigsUpdated)` walks the config index and evicts only entries whose dependent configs overlap with the changed set.\n\nConcurrent writers may both get a cache miss and generate identical configuration; `assertUnchanged` (active when `PILOT_ENABLE_UNSAFE_ASSERTIONS=true`) detects non-deterministic generation.\n\n### Generator registry\n\n`DiscoveryServer.Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator` maps type URLs (and optionally proxy-type/type-URL compound keys) to generators. At startup, Istiod registers:\n\n| Key | Generator |\n|---|---|\n| `cluster.loadassignment.v3.ClusterLoadAssignment` (EDS) | `EdsGenerator` |\n| `listener.v3.Listener` (LDS) | `ListenerGenerator` |\n| `route.v3.RouteConfiguration` (RDS) | `RouteConfigGenerator` |\n| `cluster.v3.Cluster` (CDS) | `ClusterGenerator` |\n| `secret.v3.Secret` (SDS) | `SecretGenerator` |\n| Custom proxy generators (Ztunnel, ambient) | registered on first use |\n\nThe `findGenerator()` function in `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go` resolves the most-specific generator: `metadata.Generator/typeURL` \u2192 `proxy.Type/typeURL` \u2192 `typeURL` \u2192 proxy-default.\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n**Sources:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`\n\n### Stream establishment\n\n`StreamAggregatedResources(stream)` (state-of-the-world ADS) and `DeltaAggregatedResources(stream)` (incremental xDS) are the two gRPC entry points. Both share the same lifecycle:\n\n1. **Rate-limit check** \u2014 `WaitForRequestLimit` blocks if the token bucket is exhausted (returning `codes.ResourceExhausted`).\n2. **mTLS authentication** \u2014 `s.authenticate(ctx)` extracts peer certificate SANs from gRPC metadata. Failure returns `codes.Unauthenticated`.\n3. **Connection creation** \u2014 a `Connection` struct wraps the raw gRPC stream. The connection is anonymous until the first `DiscoveryRequest` arrives with a `node` field.\n4. **Readiness guard** \u2014 if `serverReady` is false, the connection is rejected.\n\n### The `Connection` type\n\n```go\ntype Connection struct {\n    xds.Connection                // stream wrapper, push channel, watched resource state\n    node        *core.Node        // raw envoy node metadata (preserved to avoid re-marshal)\n    proxy       *model.Proxy      // fully parsed, enriched proxy object\n    deltaStream DeltaDiscoveryStream\n    deltaReqChan chan *discovery.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\n    s           *DiscoveryServer\n}\n```\n\n`xds.Connection` (in `pkg/xds`) holds:\n- The gRPC stream\n- `WatchedResources map[string]*model.WatchedResource` \u2014 per-type subscription state\n- `PushCh() chan any` \u2014 the channel through which push events are delivered to this connection's goroutine\n\n### Proxy initialization\n\n`initConnection(node, con, identities)` performs the full lifecycle in order:\n\n1. `initProxyMetadata` \u2014 parses `node.Metadata` and `node.Id` into a `model.Proxy`. Fails fast with `codes.InvalidArgument` on bad format.\n2. Cluster alias resolution \u2014 remaps the proxy's cluster ID if configured.\n3. `addCon(con.ID(), con)` \u2014 registers the connection in `adsClients` **before** completing initialization, to avoid a race with new push contexts arriving between registration and initialization.\n4. `authorize(con, identities)` \u2014 enforces RBAC rules on the peer identities.\n5. `initializeProxy(con)` \u2014 calls `computeProxyState`, discovers IP mode, assigns the default generator.\n6. `con.MarkInitialized()` \u2014 signals that the proxy is safe to push to.\n\n### Request processing\n\nEvery inbound `DiscoveryRequest` flows through `processRequest(req, con)`:\n\n- **HealthInfo requests** \u2014 dispatched to `WorkloadEntryController` for VM health-check recording; no xDS response.\n- **Debug type URLs** \u2014 answered immediately with a forced full push of the requested debug resource.\n- **Normal type URLs** \u2014 `ShouldRespond()` checks the ACK/NACK nonce logic to decide if a response is warranted. If yes, a `PushRequest{Full: true, Reason: ProxyRequest}` is built and `pushXds` is called.\n\n### Push ordering\n\n`pushConnection()` iterates over `watchedResourcesByOrder()`, which returns watched resources sorted by `PushOrder`:\n\n```go\nvar PushOrder = []string{\n    v3.ClusterType,    // CDS first \u2014 clusters must exist before listeners reference them\n    v3.EndpointType,   // EDS\n    v3.ListenerType,   // LDS\n    v3.RouteType,      // RDS\n    v3.SecretType,     // SDS\n    v3.AddressType,    // ambient workload addresses\n    v3.WorkloadType,\n    v3.WorkloadAuthorizationType,\n}\n```\n\nThis ordering is critical: an Envoy proxy will reject a listener that references a cluster it has not yet received.\n\n### `StartPush` \u2014 fleet-wide broadcast\n\n`AdsPushAll(req)` \u2192 `StartPush(req)` iterates over `AllClients()` and calls `pushQueue.Enqueue(con, req)` for every connection. `PushQueue` is a FIFO work queue with merge semantics: if a connection is already pending or in-flight, the new request is merged rather than enqueued twice. This prevents a wave of endpoint changes from generating N independent pushes per proxy.\n\n### Incremental (Delta) xDS\n\n`delta.go` implements `StreamDeltas` using `DeltaDiscoveryRequest`/`DeltaDiscoveryResponse`. In delta mode, the client sends explicit subscribe/unsubscribe resource names. `EdsGenerator.GenerateDeltas` can take advantage of this to compute only added/removed endpoints (`buildDeltaEndpoints`), reducing response payload size. For most resource types, delta falls back to state-of-the-world generation with the delta information used only to filter which resources to include.\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext \u2014 Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`\n\n### What PushContext holds\n\n`PushContext` is the immutable global snapshot of all mesh configuration, rebuilt on every full push. It is the single source of truth used during xDS generation:\n\n| Field | Content |\n|---|---|\n| `ServiceIndex` | All services, indexed by hostname, namespace, and exportTo visibility |\n| `virtualServiceIndex` | VirtualServices indexed by gateway and namespace for fast lookup |\n| `destinationRuleIndex` | DestinationRules indexed by hostname and namespace, with wildcard support |\n| `sidecarIndex` | SidecarScope objects pre-computed per namespace |\n| `gatewayIndex` | Gateways indexed by namespace |\n| `envoyFiltersByNamespace` | EnvoyFilter patches grouped by namespace |\n| `wasmPluginsByNamespace` | WasmPlugin extensions grouped by namespace |\n| `AuthnPolicies` | PeerAuthentication and RequestAuthentication |\n| `AuthzPolicies` | AuthorizationPolicy |\n| `Telemetry` | Telemetry resources |\n| `Mesh` | The global `MeshConfig` |\n| `networkMgr` | Cross-network gateway addresses |\n\n### `InitContext` and incremental rebuild\n\n`InitContext(env, oldPushContext, pushReq)` is the entry point. It is idempotent (`InitDone` atomic flag) and mutex-protected.\n\n- **Full rebuild** (`pushReq == nil` or `Forced=true`): calls `createNewContext`, which initializes every index from scratch: services \u2192 Kubernetes gateways \u2192 VirtualServices \u2192 DestinationRules \u2192 AuthN \u2192 AuthZ \u2192 Telemetry \u2192 WasmPlugins \u2192 EnvoyFilters \u2192 Gateways \u2192 SidecarScopes (last, because they depend on services and VSes).\n- **Incremental rebuild** (`updateContext`): inspects `pushReq.ConfigsUpdated` and only re-initializes the index whose config kind changed. If only `DestinationRule` changed, `initDestinationRules` runs, but `initVirtualServices` is skipped and the old index is shallow-copied. This avoids full re-index for unrelated changes.\n\nThe incremental update logic maps config kinds to dirty flags:\n\n```\nServiceEntry / DNSName       \u2192 servicesChanged\nDestinationRule              \u2192 destinationRulesChanged\nVirtualService               \u2192 virtualServicesChanged\nGateway                      \u2192 gatewayChanged\nSidecar                      \u2192 sidecarsChanged\nEnvoyFilter                  \u2192 envoyFiltersChanged\nAuthorizationPolicy          \u2192 authzChanged\nRequestAuthentication /\n  PeerAuthentication         \u2192 authnChanged\n```\n\nSidecarScope is recomputed whenever services, virtual services, destination rules, or sidecars change, because all four affect egress listener reachability.\n\n### SidecarScope and service visibility\n\n`getSidecarScope(proxy, workloadLabels)` selects or lazily computes a `SidecarScope` for the proxy's namespace. It controls which services are visible in that proxy's egress listeners. The three cases:\n\n1. **User-defined Sidecar in proxy namespace** \u2014 matched by workload selector labels. First exact match wins.\n2. **Root-namespace Sidecar** (`istio-system`) \u2014 converted to per-namespace scopes on demand, cached in `meshRootSidecarsByNamespace`.\n3. **Default scope** \u2014 `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace`, which grants access to all mesh services. Cached in `defaultSidecarsByNamespace`. Gateways use `DefaultSidecarScopeForGateway`.\n\nThe lazy caching pattern means that namespace-scoped defaults are only allocated for namespaces that actually have connected proxies.\n\n### DestinationRule resolution\n\n`destinationRule(proxyNamespace, service)` implements a four-step precedence lookup:\n\n1. Proxy's own namespace (most specific override)\n2. Service's namespace (producer policy)\n3. Root namespace (global default)\n\n`MostSpecificHostMatch` distinguishes between exact and wildcard host patterns, preferring exact matches.\n\n### Config translation: VirtualService \u2192 Envoy RouteConfiguration\n\nConfig translation is performed by generators in `pilot/pkg/networking/core/`:\n\n- **CDS** (`cds.go`): for each service visible to a proxy, `buildOutboundCluster` reads the matching `DestinationRule` from the push context to configure TLS settings, load balancing policy, connection pool, and subset-level clusters. The result is an Envoy `Cluster` proto.\n- **RDS** (`route/route.go`): `buildSidecarOutboundRouteConfig` reads `VirtualService`s from the push context via `SidecarScope.services` and `VirtualServicesForGateway`, then translates HTTP match conditions, retries, timeouts, fault injection, and mirror rules into Envoy `RouteConfiguration` protos.\n- **LDS** (`listener_builder.go`): creates virtual outbound listener per port based on the sidecar scope, selecting HTTP vs. TCP filter chains from service protocol.\n- **EDS** (`pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`): reads live endpoint shards directly from `model.EndpointIndex` (not the push context), enabling EDS to be incremental without a full push context rebuild.\n\n### Metrics and error tracking\n\n`PushContext.ProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus` accumulates per-proxy anomalies during generation (e.g., `EndpointNoPod`, `ProxyStatusClusterNoInstances`, `DuplicatedClusters`). These are written via `AddMetric(metric, key, proxyID, msg)` from inside generators. `OnConfigChange()` and `UpdateMetrics()` publish these to Prometheus gauges (e.g., `pilot_no_ip`, `pilot_duplicate_envoy_clusters`). The periodic goroutine in `DiscoveryServer` logs the `StatusJSON()` payload every 10 seconds if it changed.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n**Sources:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go`, `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\n### Kubernetes controller\n\n`Controller` (in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/`) is the Kubernetes service registry. For each cluster, one `Controller` instance is created. It watches:\n\n- `v1.Service` \u2192 `onServiceEvent` \u2192 `SvcUpdate` (tells xDS that cluster/EDS membership may change)\n- `EndpointSlice` \u2192 `endpointSliceController` \u2192 `EDSUpdate` / `EDSCacheUpdate`\n- `v1.Pod` \u2192 `PodCache` \u2192 feeds endpoint builder with pod labels and node locality\n- `v1.Node` \u2192 `onNodeEvent` \u2192 updates `nodeInfoMap` for gateway address resolution\n\nEach watcher registers handlers via `registerHandlers`, which push work items onto a rate-limited `queue.Instance`. The queue serializes changes within a cluster, preventing concurrent mutations to `servicesMap`.\n\nWhen an `EndpointSlice` event fires, `buildIstioEndpoints` constructs `model.IstioEndpoint` objects enriched with pod labels, network, locality, and service account. These are then passed to `EDSUpdate` or `EDSCacheUpdate` on the `XDSUpdater` interface (which `DiscoveryServer` satisfies).\n\n### XDSUpdater interface \u2014 the boundary between registry and xDS\n\n```go\ntype XDSUpdater interface {\n    EDSUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\n    EDSCacheUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\n    SvcUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, event Event)\n    ConfigUpdate(req *PushRequest)\n    ProxyUpdate(clusterID cluster.ID, ip string)\n    RemoveShard(shardKey ShardKey)\n}\n```\n\n`EDSUpdate` updates the `EndpointIndex` and triggers an **incremental push** (non-full `PushRequest`). Incremental pushes skip push context rebuild, update only EDS resources, and flow through the debouncer only if EDS debounce is enabled. This is how pod scale-up events propagate to envoys within milliseconds without rebuilding the entire config graph.\n\n`EDSCacheUpdate` updates `EndpointIndex` without triggering a push \u2014 used when many endpoints are changing atomically (e.g., during initial cache sync) to batch updates into a single eventual `EDSUpdate`.\n\n`SvcUpdate` is called when a Kubernetes `Service` is added/deleted. A service deletion calls `EndpointIndex.DeleteServiceShard`, and the service change triggers a **full push** (which rebuilds push context, regenerates CDS, LDS, RDS).\n\n### When service changes trigger CDS vs. EDS\n\n| Change | Push Type | Explanation |\n|---|---|---|\n| Pod added/removed (EndpointSlice update) | Incremental (EDS only) | Only load assignment changes; clusters/listeners unchanged |\n| Service added/deleted | Full push | CDS clusters must be created or removed; LDS may need new listener ports |\n| DestinationRule change | Full push | Cluster TLS/LB configuration changes; CDS must regenerate |\n| VirtualService change | Full push | Route configurations change; RDS must regenerate |\n| ServiceEntry added | Full push | New synthetic service \u2192 new clusters and routes |\n\nThe `edsNeedsPush` function in `eds.go` enforces this: it skips EDS generation for config kinds listed in `skippedEdsConfigs` (Gateway, VirtualService, AuthorizationPolicy, etc.), ensuring EDS only fires for changes that actually affect endpoint membership.\n\n### Aggregate controller\n\n`aggregate.Controller` (in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`) implements `model.ServiceDiscovery` by delegating to a slice of `registryEntry` objects. Each registry entry corresponds to one cluster (Kubernetes) or the ServiceEntry registry. Methods like `Services()`, `InstancesByPort()`, and `GetProxyServiceTargets()` iterate over all registries and merge results.\n\nFor multi-cluster scenarios, when `AddRegistry` is called for a remote cluster's Kubernetes controller, that cluster's services and endpoints become visible to the aggregate. Each `Controller` shard tags its endpoints with `ShardKey{Cluster: clusterID, Provider: Kubernetes}`, allowing `EndpointIndex` to track which shard owns which endpoints.\n\n### Multi-cluster support\n\n`Multicluster` (in `multicluster.go`) manages the lifecycle of per-cluster `kubeController` instances. It uses `multicluster.Component` to watch remote cluster Secrets (which contain kubeconfig files) and create or destroy `Controller` instances accordingly. When a cluster is removed, `kubeController.Close()`:\n\n1. Unregisters the cluster's event handlers from the aggregate controller\n2. Deletes its registry from the aggregate\n3. Triggers a full push (`ClusterUpdate` reason) so all proxies see the cluster removed\n\nThis allows Istiod to react to cluster membership changes without restarting. The `ClusterAliases` map (on `DiscoveryServer`) handles cases where a proxy connects with a cluster ID that is known under a different alias.\n\n### ServiceEntry controller\n\n`serviceentry.Controller` (in `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/`) registers itself as a config store watcher and translates `ServiceEntry` CRDs into `model.Service` + `model.IstioEndpoint` objects, then calls `EDSUpdate`/`SvcUpdate` on the `XDSUpdater`. This is how external services (databases, external APIs) and VM workloads appear in the mesh alongside Kubernetes services.\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Config Change \u2192 xDS Push\n\n```\n[K8s/CRD watch]         [Service registry event]\n       \u2502                         \u2502\nConfigUpdate(Full)        EDSUpdate / SvcUpdate\n       \u2502                         \u2502\n       \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                  \u25bc\n          pushChannel (buffered, 10)\n                  \u2502\n          debounce() goroutine\n          (merges concurrent requests, waits DebounceAfter)\n                  \u2502\n          Push(mergedPushRequest)\n                  \u2502\n          \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n          \u2502 Full push?       \u2502 Incremental (EDS)?\n          \u2502                  \u2502\n    initPushContext()    use existing PushContext\n    (rebuilds indexes    dropCacheForRequest()\n     selectively)        AdsPushAll()\n          \u2502                  \u2502\n          \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                 \u25bc\n          StartPush(req)\n          (enqueues req for every connected proxy)\n                 \u2502\n          sendPushes() / doSendPushes()\n          (concurrentPushLimit semaphore)\n                 \u2502\n          client.PushCh() <- &Event{pushRequest}\n                 \u2502\n          pushConnection(con, ev)\n          \u251c\u2500 computeProxyState(proxy, req)   [if Full]\n          \u251c\u2500 ProxyNeedsPush(proxy, req)      [skip if irrelevant]\n          \u2514\u2500 for each watched resource (ordered CDS\u2192EDS\u2192LDS\u2192RDS):\n               pushXds(con, watchedResource, req)\n               \u251c\u2500 findGenerator(typeURL)\n               \u251c\u2500 gen.Generate(proxy, w, req)  [may cache hit or miss]\n               \u2514\u2500 xds.Send(con, DiscoveryResponse)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\n### 1. Custom resource generators\n\nRegister a `model.XdsResourceGenerator` (or `XdsDeltaResourceGenerator`) in `DiscoveryServer.Generators`. The key format `\"<proxyType>/<typeURL>\"` allows per-proxy-type overrides. This is how Ztunnel (`Ztunnel` proxy type) gets completely different configuration from sidecar proxies for the same type URLs.\n\n### 2. EnvoyFilter patching\n\nAfter generation, each generator applies `MergedEnvoyFilterWrapper` patches from the push context. Patches can add, merge, or remove fields at specific listener/cluster/route filter chain points. This is the primary mechanism for customizing generated Envoy config without modifying Pilot source code.\n\n### 3. WasmPlugin extensions\n\n`WasmPlugin` resources are loaded into the push context and applied by the networking layer as `wasm` HTTP filters. Each plugin specifies a selector, phase, and priority, so multiple plugins compose predictably.\n\n### 4. External service registries\n\nAny component that implements `model.ServiceDiscovery` can be registered with the aggregate controller via `AddRegistry`. MCP (Mesh Configuration Protocol) sources, for example, can inject synthetic services this way.\n\n### 5. `ProxyNeedsPush` hook\n\n`DiscoveryServer.ProxyNeedsPush func(proxy *model.Proxy, req *model.PushRequest) (*model.PushRequest, bool)` is called for every proxy before any generation work. It can completely skip a push (`bool=false`) or narrow the `ConfigsUpdated` set. The default `DefaultProxyNeedsPush` implements the sidecar scope optimization: if none of the changed configs are reachable from the proxy's sidecar scope, the push is skipped.\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Config validation errors\nIstio CRDs are validated by the admission webhook before reaching the config store. If invalid configuration reaches Pilot anyway (e.g., from a file source), `initVirtualServices` / `initDestinationRules` may log warnings and skip the offending resource. The proxy status metric `DuplicatedDomains` captures rejected VirtualServices.\n\n### Push context rebuild failures\n`createNewContext` and `updateContext` do not return errors; individual sub-initializers log errors and best-effort continue. A malformed DestinationRule will be logged and skipped, leaving the previous rule in effect.\n\n### Push generation errors\nIf `gen.Generate()` returns an error, `pushXds` logs it and returns the error to `pushConnection`, which returns the error to the connection's stream goroutine, closing the stream. The proxy will reconnect and re-subscribe.\n\n### Send failures\n`xds.Send(con, resp)` errors are classified by `recordSendError`: gRPC `codes.Canceled` and `codes.Unavailable` (normal stream close) are silently dropped; other errors are warned. Any error closes the push cycle for that resource on that connection.\n\n### Proxy disconnects\n`closeConnection(con)` removes the connection from `adsClients` and calls `WorkloadEntryController.OnDisconnect`, which may delete the proxy's `WorkloadEntry` if it was auto-registered.\n\n### Cache token staleness\nThe `lruCache.token` field is incremented on `Clear`/`ClearAll`. Each cached entry records the token at write time. On `Add`, if the current token is greater than the entry's token, the write is silently dropped, preventing stale results from a slow goroutine overwriting fresh results from a faster concurrent push.\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files Reference\n\n| File | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go` | `DiscoveryServer` struct, debounce loop, push orchestration, cache management |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` | `Connection` type, `Stream()`, `processRequest()`, `pushConnection()`, `StartPush()`, `AdsPushAll()` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go` | Delta (incremental) xDS stream handler |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go` | Generator lookup (`findGenerator`), `pushXds`, `xdsNeedsPush` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/pushqueue.go` | `PushQueue` \u2014 merge-on-enqueue work queue |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go` | `EdsGenerator`, `EDSUpdate`, `EDSCacheUpdate`, `SvcUpdate` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go` | `ClusterGenerator` entry point |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go` | `ListenerGenerator` entry point |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go` | `RouteGenerator` entry point |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` | `PushContext`, `InitContext`, `updateContext`, `XDSUpdater` interface, `PushRequest`, `TriggerReason` |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/typed_xds_cache.go` | `typedXdsCache`, `lruCache`, config-indexed eviction |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go` | `EndpointIndex`, shard management |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` | `SidecarScope`, `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace` |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go` | Kubernetes `Controller`, service/endpoint/pod watchers |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/multicluster.go` | `Multicluster`, per-cluster controller lifecycle |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go` | Aggregate `Controller`, multi-registry fan-out |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/` | ServiceEntry \u2192 `model.Service` translation |\n| `pilot/pkg/networking/core/` | CDS/LDS/RDS config translation from push context to Envoy protos |\n",

# Istio Pilot Discovery Service: Architecture Document

## Overview

Pilot's discovery subsystem is the core of Istio's control plane. It translates high-level mesh configuration (VirtualService, DestinationRule, ServiceEntry, etc.) into Envoy's native xDS resources (CDS, LDS, RDS, EDS) and streams them to every proxy in the mesh over long-lived gRPC connections. Four interlocking components make this work:

1. **DiscoveryServer** — the gRPC server and orchestrator
2. **ADS/Connection** — the per-proxy stream handler
3. **PushContext** — an immutable configuration snapshot built once per change event
4. **Service Registry** — the Kubernetes and ServiceEntry watchers that feed discovery data

---

## 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server

**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`

### What it owns

`DiscoveryServer` is the singleton struct that implements Envoy's `AggregatedDiscoveryService` gRPC interface. It is the authoritative owner of:

- `adsClients map[string]*Connection` — the live set of connected Envoy proxies, keyed by connection ID
- `pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest` — raw incoming change notifications (from config watches, service registry, JWT resolver, etc.)
- `pushQueue *PushQueue` — ordered work queue for per-proxy push dispatch after debouncing
- `Cache model.XdsCache` — typed LRU cache for already-generated xDS resources
- `concurrentPushLimit chan struct{}` — semaphore that caps parallel in-flight pushes (controlled by `PILOT_PUSH_THROTTLE`)
- `RequestRateLimit *rate.Limiter` — token bucket that throttles new gRPC connection acceptance

### Initialization and startup

`NewDiscoveryServer` creates the struct and wires its fields. No resources are served until `CachesSynced()` is called, which sets `serverReady = true`. Until that point, every inc
... (truncated)
